22/* The conversion table to UCS4 has almost no holes. It can be generated with:
23
24 egrep '^0x' /mnt/cdrom/unix/mappings/eastasia/gb/gb2312.txt |
25 perl tab.pl
26
27 where tab.pl is:
28 ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
29 $n=0;
30 while (<>) {
31 local($gb, $ucs4, %rest) = split;
32 local($u)=hex($ucs4);
33 local($g)=hex($gb);
34 printf ("\n ") if ($n % 4 eq 0);
35 ++$n;
36 printf (" [0x%04x] = 0x%04x,",
37 int(($g - 0x2121) / 256) * 94 + (($g - 0x2121) & 0xff), $u);
38 }
39 printf ("\n");
40 ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
41 */

2231 local($ucs4, $gb, %rest) = split;
2232 local($u)=hex($ucs4);
2233 local($g)=hex($gb);

2235 ++$n;
2236 printf (" [0x%04x] = \"\\x%02x\\x%02x\",", $u - 0x4e00,
2237 $g < 0x100 ? $g : int($g/256), $g < 0x100 ? 0 : $g&255);

4501/* The table can be created using
4502
4503 egrep '^0x' /mnt/cdrom/unix/mappings/eastasia/gb/gb2312.txt |
4504 awk '{ print $2, $1 }' | sort | egrep '^0xFF[0-5]' | perl tab.pl
4505
4506 where tab.pl is
4507

4509 $n=0;
4510 while (<>) {
4511 local($ucs4, $gb, %rest) = split;
4512 local($u)=hex($ucs4);
4513 local($g)=hex($gb);
4514 printf ("\n ") if ($n % 3 == 0);
4515 ++$n;
4516 printf (" [0x%04x] = \"\\x%02x\\x%02x\",", $u - 0xff01,
4517 $g < 0x100 ? $g : int($g/256), $g < 0x100 ? 0 : $g&255);
4518 }
4519 printf ("\n");
